<div id="review_907079973" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/907079973" />
    <a title="Ana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28781546-ana"><img alt="Ana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450253963p2/28781546.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/907079973?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana" href="/user/show/28781546-ana">Ana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19098600-the-indian-in-the-cupboard">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28781546-ana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28781546-ana?shelf=european-literature">european-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28781546-ana?shelf=british-literature">british-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28781546-ana?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28781546-ana?shelf=indigenous-character">indigenous-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28781546-ana?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28781546-ana?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer907079973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7837596376734698478">While I can understand that the intent of the book was to entertain and educate young people about Native Americans, I just can't shake the feeling that this book is too creepy to enjoy unless you have nostalgia for it and know very little about Native peoples history. Making a member of a different race a toy that belongs to a white child is problematic and just because Omri is nice to his come-to-life-toy doesn't make it okay to minimize the conflict between the settlers and the natives. Also </span>
  <span id="freeText7837596376734698478" style="display:none">While I can understand that the intent of the book was to entertain and educate young people about Native Americans, I just can't shake the feeling that this book is too creepy to enjoy unless you have nostalgia for it and know very little about Native peoples history. Making a member of a different race a toy that belongs to a white child is problematic and just because Omri is nice to his come-to-life-toy doesn't make it okay to minimize the conflict between the settlers and the natives. Also the writing was unimpressive and the plot was bland so this book was a chore to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7837596376734698478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6S3uhalnRp9ynWVTnP3lajB9bMYUNEiDe/NZGzl3Icja+6stXvWgU6stQL8yVTSmuJybHlH66ezW40p0QozaMQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QQmeAnX7L5pqybjHCCGVrvuyDl60FpJM26ytc57hWcdy39uqgmnJVrN5nSumiURic1P5hvHYMyN2vL4c5RqiPg==')})
  }

Mario, the son of Mama and Papa Bellini, proprietors of the subway-station newsstand, had only heard the sound once. What was this new, strangely musical chirping? None other than the mellifluous leg-rubbing of the somewhat disoriented Chester Cricket from Connecticut. Attracted by the irresistible smell of liverwurst, Chester had foolishly jumped into the picnic basket of some unsuspecting New Yorkers on a junket to the country. Despite the insect\'s wurst intentions, he ends up in a pile of dirt in Times Square. Mario is elated to find Chester. He begs his parents to let him keep the shiny insect in the newsstand, assuring his bug-fearing mother that crickets are harmless, maybe even good luck. What ensues is an altogether captivating spin on the city mouse/country mouse story, as Chester adjusts to the bustle of the big city. Despite the cricket\'s comfortable matchbox bed (with Kleenex sheets); the fancy, seven-tiered pagoda cricket cage from Sai Fong\'s novelty shop; tasty mulberry leaves; the jolly company of Tucker Mouse and Harry Cat; and even his new-found fame as &quot;the most famous musician in New York City,&quot; Chester begins to miss his peaceful life in the Connecticut countryside. The Cricket in Times Square--a Newbery Honor Book in 1961--is charmingly illustrated by the well-loved Garth Williams, and the tiniest details of this elegantly spun, vividly told, surprisingly suspenseful tale will stick with children for years and years.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/72237.Lynne_Reid_Banks">About Lynne Reid Banks</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/72237.Lynne_Reid_Banks"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1202838464p3/72237.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/72237.Lynne_Reid_Banks">Lynne Reid Banks
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10881125485909823239">Lynne Reid Banks is a British author of books for children and adults. She has written forty books, including the best-selling children's novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/125404.The_Indian_in_the_Cupboard' title='The Indian in the Cupboard' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Indian in the Cupboard</a>, which has sold over 10 million copies and been made into a film.<br/>Banks was born in London, the only child of James and Muriel Reid Banks. She was evacuated to Saskatoon, Saskatchewan, Canada during World War II but returned after</span>
  <span id="freeText10881125485909823239" style="display:none">Lynne Reid Banks is a British author of books for children and adults. She has written forty books, including the best-selling children's novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/125404.The_Indian_in_the_Cupboard" title="The Indian in the Cupboard" rel="nofollow noopener">The Indian in the Cupboard</a>, which has sold over 10 million copies and been made into a film.<br />Banks was born in London, the only child of James and Muriel Reid Banks. She was evacuated to Saskatoon, Saskatchewan, Canada during World War II but returned after the war was over. She attended St Teresa's School in Surrey. Prior to becoming a writer Banks was an actress, and also worked as a television journalist in Britain, one of the first women to do so. Her first novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/960246.The_L_Shaped_Room" title="The L-Shaped Room" rel="nofollow noopener">The L-Shaped Room</a>, was published in 1960.<br />In 1962 Banks emigrated to Israel, where she taught for eight years on an Israeli kibbutz Yasur. In 1965 she married Chaim Stephenson, with whom she had three sons. Although the family returned to England in 1971 and Banks now lives in Dorset with her husband, the influence of her time in Israel can be seen in some of her books which are set partially or mainly on kibbutzim.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10881125485909823239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
